Friday evening in the Brooks' basement was a buzz of new, academic energy. The Group of 8, home for the weekend, was gathered around the large dining table, their laptops open. The English 102 group project was their main focus: a proposal to fix a problem on the CPI campus.

"The accessibility idea is brilliant, Jordan," Hannah said, "but where do we even start? The campus is huge."

"We start here," Jordan said, tapping his laptop. He had pulled up the university's official accessibility website. "Here's the map they provide for students with disabilities. It shows ramps, elevators, and push button doors."

The group leaned in. The map was, to be blunt, awful. It was crudely drawn, looking more like a cartoon than a functional guide.

"Look at this," Jordan said, zooming in. "This icon for a push button door isn't even near the actual entrance. We know that. We use it every day.".

He then scrolled to the part of campus where their old dorm, The Old Lady on the Hill, used to be. "And look. Bennett Hall. It's just... a building. There's nothing here."

"What do you mean?" Mark asked, leaning in.

"Bennett Hall had an elevator that let you cut through the building to get up the hill," Jordan explained, his frustration growing. "It was a major accessibility route, but it's not marked on the map at all. There's no explanation that a student ID could access the first and second floor entrances to use it". He pointed to the corner of the PDF. "And look, the map is old. It came out when Bennett was still open, so it *should* be on here".

He sat back, a look of sudden, sharp clarity on his face. "This is it," he said, his voice full of a new, focused energy. "This is our proposal."

"What, to get them to fix the map?" Lauren asked.

"Not just the map. The *information*," Jordan said. "We can't ask the university for millions of dollars to build new ramps and elevators. That's not a realistic proposal for one semester". "But this? Updating a PDF? Fixing the icons? Writing clear, accurate descriptions of *existing* accessible routes, like the one at Bennett? That's not expensive. That's just... work. It's something that can be easily fixed".

A wave of unanimous agreement went through the group. It was the perfect idea: focused, achievable, and deeply personal. This would be their project.

Megan, who had been sitting with them at the table, clapped her hands together, her face a mask of pure pride. "Jordan, that is brilliant!" she cheered. "Yes! That's exactly what you should do! People with disabilities deserve to succeed in school without having to guess where a ramp or an elevator is. You show them how to fix it!".

### Part 6: The Project and the Pact

The basement hummed with a quiet, focused energy. While Daniel and Laura cooked dinner upstairs, the Group of 8 was clustered around the dining table, their laptops open. This was their first official work session for the English 102 final project.

"Okay," Zoe said, acting as the project manager. "We need a rough draft of the outline by Monday. I'll create the shared document".

Jordan, energized, was at the head of the table in his wheelchair, directing the conversation. "The introduction has to define the problem. It's not just a bad map. It's a failure of information. Students can't use resources they don't know exist."

"He's right," Mark added. "We can propose a new, interactive map that uses a clean database. It's not even hard. The current one is just lazy."

Megan sat on the sofa nearby, listening to them work, her heart swelling with pride. She was their biggest cheerleader, and she loved seeing them all, especially Jordan, so engaged and passionate. She knew they were building a proposal that could genuinely help people.

Just as Zoe typed the final bullet point for their outline, Daniel's voice called from the top of the stairs. "Dinner's coming down!"

The group let out a happy, hungry cheer. Daniel and Laura came down with the feast: baked salmon, brown rice, and roasted asparagus. It was a heart-healthy meal for everyone, a new standard the whole family had embraced in solidarity with Jordan.

They all gathered in the living room area, balancing plates on their laps. The conversation immediately turned to a recap of the day.

"You're lucky you were here, J," Mark grumbled. "The 6:00 AM bus was so packed, I thought I was going to have to stand in the aisle."

"And my last lecture was a total snoozefest," Madison added.

"It was just... quiet here," Jordan said, looking at Megan with a grateful smile. "It was too quiet until Megan started her workday. I'm glad you guys are all back."

As they talked, the bond between Jordan and Megan was visible to everyone. He listened intently to a story she was telling, his gaze warm and focused. She laughed, her hand resting on his arm in an easy, familiar gesture.

Zoe, ever the analyst, saw this new data point. She caught Aubrie's eye from across the room and gave a subtle tilt of her head toward Megan and Jordan, a silent query: *Are you processing this?*

Aubrie already knew. She saw the way Jordan looked at Megan, and she saw the happy, sisterly affection Megan gave him. Aubrie's heart was happy. She turned her gaze to Megan, and when she looked over, Aubrie gave her a slow, brilliant, and completely unambiguous smile. It was a silent, powerful signal: *You are welcome. If you want this, the door is open.*

Megan, catching the look, blushed and quickly looked down at her plate, her heart hammering. She couldn't. She was too old. It wouldn't be right.

Aubrie, seeing the blush, just kept smiling. She knew the seeds were planted. She leaned her head on Jordan's shoulder, her happiness complete. The rest of the pact, seeing the exchange, felt it too. They were all happy to be home for the weekend, back in their fortress, together with Jordan.

### Part 7: The Shower Protocol

The evening wound down, and the happy chaos of the group’s return settled into a sleepy, domestic peace. It was time for Jordan to get ready for bed.

"Alright, J," Hannah said, moving toward the bathroom. "Time to get you washed up."

"Actually," Aubrie said, cutting her off with a warm, pointed smile. She looked across the room at Megan, who was cleaning up the last of the dinner dishes. "Megan, you were so incredible with him last night, and you're so strong. Would you mind taking the lead on this tonight?"

Megan looked up, feeling the eyes of the entire pact on her. She knew this was more than a request for help; it was an invitation. It was the pact of five, seeing her internal conflict, and actively giving her permission. Her heart hammered, but she nodded, trying to look casual. "Of course. No problem at all."

She wheeled Jordan into the accessible basement bathroom. "Alright, transfer protocol," she said, positioning his chair next to the shower bench. "Ready?"

In one surprisingly strong and fluid motion, Megan lifted Jordan from his chair and settled him securely on the bench. It was a move that usually required both Hannah and Lauren to coordinate, but Megan managed it safely on her own.

Zoe, who had followed them in with the discharge binder, made a mental note. *New protocol: Megan is the primary agent for all high-risk transfers.*

Megan began the clinical act of care, following the strict rules from the binder. She meticulously kept the incision on his chest dry while she carefully washed his hair and body. Her mind was a whirl. *This is just care. It's medical. He's my brother. He's Zoe's family.* But as she performed the task with a gentle, respectful hand, she felt that now-familiar, dangerous flutter in her stomach. She was deeply happy to be trusted this much, but she immediately reinforced her internal boundary. *This is a sister's job. This is not romantic.*

Jordan, for his part, was acutely aware of her. He could sense her conflicted energy. He knew she liked him; he'd felt it since the night of his meltdown. But he was afraid to say anything, terrified of breaking the "sister" boundary she had established. He decided to test the waters, just a little.

"You know," he said, his voice casual, "when Aubrie or Madi help me with this, they usually just hop in and take their own shower after. Since they're already in the bathroom and all".

Megan's hands froze on his shoulder. A deep, hot blush flooded her entire body. She was completely flustered. The invitation was implied, but the 8-year age gap screamed in her head. She was unable to answer.

"Oh, I... I..." she stammered, immediately defaulting to her caregiver role. "Okay, let's get you rinsed off."

She quickly finished washing him, helped him get dried, and into his pajamas. She was quiet, her mind racing. She wheeled him back out into the main room, where the rest of the Group of 8 was waiting.

They knew something was changing. The energy between Jordan and Megan was palpable and awkward. Jordan looked embarrassed, worried he'd pushed too hard. Megan looked like she'd been caught.

Zoe, the analyst, processed the data: 1. Megan is conflicted. 2. Jordan is interested. 3. The pact is supportive. 4. The only barrier is Megan's internal script.

Zoe decided to apply a logical override. She walked over to her sister.

"Megan," Zoe said, her voice clear and kind, "you're welcome to explore your feelings".

Megan's blush, which had just started to fade, returned with a vengeance. She was now completely exposed, but also, for the first time, given explicit, logical *permission*.

### Part 8: The Elephant in the Room

It was finally time for bed. Megan, seeing the Group of 8 start their wind-down routines, knew it was time for her to find her own space. She wanted to stay in the basement, close to the warmth and energy of the group, hoping what Zoe had said earlier about exploring her feelings was true.

She walked over to the sectional sofa and picked up the pillow and blanket that were already draped there. She wanted to be near Jordan, but she didn't want to intrude. She glanced at the massive king-sized bed, the space he had carved out with the pact. She knew Aubrie was the one who slept in bed with him.

For a fleeting moment, Megan pictured herself climbing into that bed with them. *No, scratch that,* she thought immediately, her cheeks flushing. *That would be asking way too much*. She wouldn't push her luck. The sofa was safe.

"Alright, team, we're heading up," Mark announced. He and Hannah said their goodnights, gave Jordan and Megan their hugs, and headed upstairs to Zoe's old room.

Before being wheeled to his own bed, Jordan stopped in front of Megan. "Goodnight, Megan," he said. "Thank you... for today."

"Goodnight, Jordan," she replied, her voice soft.

She stepped forward to give him his goodnight hug. As his arms wrapped around her, the hug felt different. It wasn't just sisterly; it was charged, and it lingered. The five women of the pact watched the exchange, and to them, it was obviously romantic. They exchanged small, knowing smiles. They were all okay with it.

As he held her, Jordan debated kissing her. He wanted to. But he hesitated, his old anxieties flaring. It was too soon. He decided against it and pulled back, giving her a small, shaky smile.

"Time for bed, J," Zoe said, her voice gentle.

She wheeled Jordan into the master bedroom area, and the other four women of the pact followed. Zoe closed the door, giving them privacy.

The five of them began their own bedtime routine, but the tension was thick.

"Okay," Madison said, sitting on the edge of the king bed. "We have to talk about the elephant in the room".

"Megan," Aubrie said, her voice soft but clear.

Jordan looked at them. "She... she's amazing."

"We know, J," Lauren said. "We see the way you look at her. And we see the way she looks at you".

Zoe, ever the analyst, got straight to the point. "The data is conclusive. There is mutual romantic interest between you and my sister. This is a new, positive variable."

Jordan looked at Aubrie, his oldest fear still present. "But... are you sure? You're all... okay with it?"

Aubrie took his hand. "Jordan, look at me. We are prepared to welcome Megan into the pact if she wants. That's the whole point. We love you. We trust you. And we are starting to really love her. She fits".

"She really does," Sarah added. "She's... she's one of us."

"So," Madison grinned, "if she wants in... we're good with it. The only question is, are *you*?".

Jordan looked at the faces of the five women he loved. He thought about Megan, her strength, her kindness, her butterflies.

"Yes," he said, his voice firm. "Now that I know you're all ready to include her... I would want that. Very much".

Aubrie smiled, her heart full. "Good. Then the pact of six is officially on the table. Now we just have to wait for her to be ready to ask."

### Part 9: A New Dawn

Saturday morning. Jordan woke slowly, pulled from the most beautiful, vivid dream he had ever had.

He wasn't in the basement, and his chest didn't hurt. He was sitting on the sofa, his body healthy and whole. He was surrounded by his entire pact, all six women. Aubrie, Madison, Zoe, Lauren, Sarah, and Megan were all there, their faces glowing, their hands resting on their own round, pregnant bellies. They were looking over blueprints for the nursery, all of them talking and laughing together. Daniel and Laura were there, beaming with excitement, holding up catalogs for cribs. There was no jealousy, no fear... only a profound, perfect peace.

He opened his eyes.

The dream dissolved. He was back in the basement, in the king-sized bed. The first sensation he felt was the familiar, dull ache in his sternum. A profound wave of sadness washed over him. It wasn't real. He was sad to wake up, to be pulled from a reality that had felt so perfect.

"Hey..." a soft voice whispered.

Aubrie was awake beside him, spooning him carefully, her arm draped over his side. She had felt him stir, had sensed the deep, shuddering sigh he let out. She shifted to look at his face in the dim morning light and saw the unmistakable track of a tear on his cheek.

"Jordan? What's wrong?" she asked, her voice full of immediate, quiet concern.

He turned his head on the pillow, his eyes shining. "I had a dream," he whispered, his voice thick with emotion. "It was... us. All of us. In the new house. And everyone... you, Madi, Zoe, Lauren, Sarah... and Megan... you were all..." He couldn't finish the sentence, but she understood.

"You were all pregnant," he finally managed. "And you were all so happy. There was no jealousy. It was just... our family."

Aubrie’s heart filled to bursting. She smiled, a brilliant, radiant smile as she processed his words. He was sad because he *wanted* that reality. He was sad because he had woken up *from* it.

"Oh, Jordan," she whispered, her face a picture of pure bliss. She leaned in, kissing his cheek. "Don't be sad. Don't you see? That wasn't just a dream. That's the *plan*."

She saw the look in his eyes when he'd said Megan's name. She'd seen it last night, too. "Megan belongs with us," Aubrie said, her voice a soft, steady promise. "I know it. And I'm ready to welcome her. We all are".

It felt like just yesterday she had walked into Room 214 and found a terrified boy in the middle of an autistic meltdown. A boy who didn't even know how to get dressed by himself. And now... now he was a man, her partner, dreaming of a future with *all* of them. A man who knew how to ask for help when he needed it.

She brushed the tear from his face. "That future? It's real. We're building it. But it starts today."

She smiled, her energy bright and new. "And today, we have a plan. You are going out to breakfast". "Your first meal out since the hospital. The whole family is going—all eight of us, plus Mom, Dad, and Megan".

"Now," she said, carefully sliding out of the bed, "let's get you ready to face your beautiful Saturday morning".

### Part 10: The First Outing

The plan was set, and the energy in the basement was bright and excited. The full Group of 17 was mobilizing for Jordan's first restaurant meal since his surgery. Daniel and Laura coordinated the convoy.

"Okay," Daniel said, "Megan, you take your car. Jordan, you'll ride with her". He knew his son would feel more independent in a regular sedan. "Aubrie, Madison, you two ride with Megan". The rest of the family would pile into the minivan.

Getting into Megan's car was a careful process, but Jordan, now practiced in his transfers and still on sternal precautions, managed it with her help. He settled into the front passenger seat, heart pillow firmly against his chest, and buckled in. Aubrie and Madison climbed into the back seat.

The small convoy pulled out of Geneva Street and headed for Blacksburg, the drive a welcome change of scenery for Jordan. He looked out the window, just happy to be out of the house, his mind focused on the simple, wonderful prospect of a meal he didn't have to eat on a sofa.

As they drove up U.S. 460, Aubrie leaned forward from the back seat, her voice warm. "Megan, I'm so glad you're able to be with Jordan during the day. It really puts my mind at ease knowing he's not alone".

"Me too," Madison added, chiming in. "It's perfect. He needs someone he can trust."

Megan felt a hot blush creep up her neck. She gripped the steering wheel, her knuckles white. She could hear the subtext, the words they weren't saying. This was more than just gratitude; this felt like... permission. It felt like his two "safe people" were trying to *imply* that she was welcome to get romantically close to him, but they were too scared to just come out and say it. Her heart hammered in her chest.

She glanced at Jordan. He was oblivious to the subtext, just looking forward to breakfast, a calm, happy smile on his face.

"Oh, it's... it's no bother at all," Megan finally stammered. "I'm just happy to help. He's family."

She kept her eyes on the road, her mind a confusing whirl of hope and her own "I'm too old" anxiety.

They pulled into the parking lot of "The Smokin’ Anvil," a small, popular breakfast-and-lunch spot in Blacksburg. The rest of the family was already parking. Jordan just looked at the restaurant, his stomach rumbling. He was ready to eat.

### Part 11: The Smokin' Anvil

The Smokin' Anvil was bustling with the late Saturday morning crowd, but the family convoy, eleven strong, managed to secure a large rectangular table near the back. Jordan was placed at the head of the table in his wheelchair, with Aubrie on his left and Madison on his right. Megan, smiling, sat directly across from him. The rest of the family filled in the sides: Daniel sat next to Aubrie, Laura next to Madison, and Mark, Hannah, Zoe, Lauren, and Sarah filled the remaining chairs, creating a loud, happy, protective bubble.

A cheerful waitress took their orders. Jordan, savoring his first meal out, ordered scrambled eggs with American cheese, bacon, wheat toast, and an orange juice. The others ordered a mix of breakfast platters—Daniel and Mark opted for the "Anvil Slam," while Megan, still in solidarity, ordered a fruit and yogurt parfait.

The family was talking and laughing, everyone proud of Jordan for how far he had come in just one short year. He was in the middle of telling Megan a story when the bistro's front bell chimed.

A woman entered, and Jordan’s blood ran cold.

He froze, his fork clattering against his plate. It was *her*. The same height, the same build, the same dark hair. It was Aubrie Sinclair. His breath hitched, and he instinctively gripped Aubrie's hand under the table, his knuckles turning white.

"Jordan? What's wrong?" Aubrie whispered, seeing the color drain from his face.

Megan, sitting across from him, saw his eyes lock on the door, and her own "big sister" defenses went on high alert.

Before Jordan's mind could fully process the perceived threat and spiral into a meltdown, the woman at the counter spoke to the cashier. "I'll just have a large coffee to go, please," she said, her voice a high, cheerful Southern drawl.

It wasn't her. The voice was totally different. It was just a random coincidence.

Jordan let out a long, shaky breath, his heart still hammering. He felt Aubrie rubbing circles on his hand. He was okay. He was safe.

He looked at the woman again as she paid for her coffee and left. She was just a stranger. He took a sip of his orange juice, forcing his hands to steady. He did not want this to defeat him. He wanted to live his life.

He knew, in that moment, that even if his mother *had* walked in, he was not afraid anymore. He looked around the table. He had this incredible family, all of them sitting right here with him, ready to defend him in every way that mattered. They had decided he was one of them. He looked at Aubrie, Madison, Zoe, Lauren, and Sarah—his pact of five. He looked at Megan. He knew for a fact that all of them were his safe people. He looked at Daniel and Laura. They *were* his parents. Not his biological mother. Not his biological father, who had been killed before he was born. He looked at Mark and Hannah. He trusted them unconditionally.

His fear, unanchored by his old programming, simply dissolved.

He finished the last bite of his scrambled eggs and turned to Mark. "Mark," he said, his voice clear. "I want to start working out again. When can we resume the exercise protocol?"

Mark smiled, but shook his head. "Not just yet, J. We're not doing *that* protocol. I've got a better idea, and it should be in that thick discharge binder Zoe's been guarding".

Jordan looked confused.

"My uncle went through the same thing, remember?" Mark explained. "You're on sternal precautions, so you can't just go to a gym. In a week or two, a home health nurse is going to start visiting to make sure your recovery is on track". "And then, you'll start Cardiac Rehab".

"Cardiac... what?"

"Cardiac Rehab," Mark repeated. "It's exactly what it sounds like. You'll go to a special facility a few times a week, and you'll do exercises under the direct supervision of nurses. They'll have you hooked up to a heart monitor, watching you the whole time to make sure you're safe. It's how you'll get your strength back, man. It's how you'll resume living your life".

## Chapter 14: The Comeback

### Part 1: The Big Day

The 5:15 AM alarms were a harsh, digital intrusion, but they were now a familiar part of the day. Jordan woke on the new king-sized bed, Aubrie's steady breathing a comfort beside him. Today was different, though. He wasn't just facing another day of recovery; he was going *back*. Today was his English 102 presentation.

He carefully turned his head, wincing at the familiar pull in his sternum. Across the room, on the sectional sofa, Megan was just starting to stir, pushing her hair out of her face. A warm, happy feeling spread through his chest. He was so happy to see her again, that she was *here*. He knew she was sleeping on the sofa because she didn't want to intrude on the king bed, the space he shared with the pact, but just having her in the same room felt right.

The basement was a flurry of activity as the Group of 8 got ready for their 6:00 AM bus. The care protocol was efficient. Hannah and Lauren helped him with the careful pivot transfer from the bed to his wheelchair, while Aubrie and Madison helped him get washed and dressed for his big day on campus.

"You ready for this, J?" Mark asked, giving him a firm, one-armed brotherly hug. "You're gonna kill it."

The pact of five came next, one by one, for their romantic kisses and hugs.

"We'll save you a seat right in the front row," Madison whispered.

"We'll be waiting for you," Aubrie added, giving him one last, lingering kiss. "I'm so proud of you."

They grabbed their bags and, with a final chorus of "Good luck!" and "See you later!", the Group of 8 headed up the stairs, leaving for CPI.

The basement was suddenly, profoundly quiet.

"Well," Megan's cheerful voice cut through the silence. "Looks like it's just you and me for a bit."

She came over, her eyes bright. "Breakfast first, then we can worry about your presentation. How are you feeling?"

"Nervous," Jordan admitted, "but... good. Ready."

"Good." She smiled and went to the kitchenette. She followed their established routine, making them both a heart-healthy breakfast of scrambled eggs and wheat toast with jelly, and pouring two glasses of orange juice. She sat at the dining table with him, her presence a familiar, comforting start to his important day.

### Part 2: The Return to Campus

Later that day, it was time to go. Megan, who had taken a paid personal day from work just for this, helped Jordan transfer from the sofa to his wheelchair. He was nervous, but the excitement of returning to campus was a powerful motivator.

She helped him into the front passenger seat of her car. He was glad Megan was the one driving him. He was really starting to enjoy her company, just as much as he enjoyed being with the five women of the pact. He found himself wanting her to join them, to make the pact of five a pact of six, but he had no idea how to even word that thought. It felt impossible, so he pushed the confusing feeling down.

Megan placed his heart pillow firmly against his chest, and he held it as she buckled the seatbelt over it. As they pulled out of Geneva Street, he looked forward to just seeing CPI again.

Megan had purchased a visitor's parking pass ahead of time, and she hung Jordan's new handicap placard from her rearview mirror as they arrived on campus. The university was busy, and Jordan’s anxiety spiked.

"It's going to be hard to find a spot," he murmured, scanning the packed lots near his classroom building.

"We'll find one," Megan said calmly. Just as she spoke, the taillights of a car in a handicap spot right near the main walkway flashed on. The car pulled out, and Megan slid the car in. "And there it is," she grinned. "Perfect timing".

She got out and retrieved his wheelchair from the trunk, helping him with the careful, slow transfer from the car seat. Jordan, clutching his heart pillow tightly to brace his sternum, settled into his chair.

"Okay," he said, getting his bearings and looking at the network of sidewalks. "We need to go up this path, and then take the first left...".

Megan chuckled softly, cutting him off. She stepped behind his wheelchair, her hands settling on the grips.

"Jordan, I probably should have mentioned this earlier," she said, a playful smile in her voice. "I'm a CPI alumnus. I know this campus like the back of my hand. All you have to do is tell me which building we're going to. I'll get us there".

Jordan looked up at her, surprised and impressed. "Walton Hall," he said.

"Walton Hall it is," Megan said, pushing him forward. "Let's go show them what you've got."

### Part 3: Arrival at Walton

Megan navigated the campus pathways with practiced ease, pushing Jordan’s wheelchair right to the accessible entrance of Walton Hall. As they entered the familiar lobby, Jordan’s heart gave a happy jolt. The rest of the Group of 8 was already there, clustered by the doors to the lecture hall, waiting for him.

"He’s here!" Madison cheered softly.

They all converged on him, their faces bright with smiles. The hellos were a careful, practiced ritual. The women of the pact gave him gentle, loving kisses, and Mark and Hannah gave him soft, one-armed hugs, all of them extremely careful of his chest.

"You ready for this, J?" Mark asked, his voice full of pride.

"I'm ready," Jordan said, and he meant it. He was so "happy to see everyone" and just to be "back on campus," even for a little while.

A few minutes later, Dr. Evans, the professor, opened the classroom door. "Alright, folks, it's 9:00 AM. Let's get started. The first group can set up.".

"That's us," Zoe said, picking up her bag.

"Okay," Megan said, squeezing Jordan's shoulders. "You're up. I'll be right out here in the lobby waiting for you when you're done".

She found a quiet bench to sit on, and Jordan wheeled himself into the lecture hall, his family surrounding him as they moved to the front of the room. He was nervous, but he was also deeply happy. He understood the conditions needed to be controlled for his safety. He knew he wasn't here for the day. He was here just for class, and as soon as it was over, he would head home with Megan. It was a perfect, surgical strike, and he was ready to nail his part of the presentation.

### Part 4: The Presentation

The group presented third. Zoe led, her voice clear and analytical as she laid out the project's parameters and the flaws in the university's current information system. Mark followed, briefly explaining the technical back-end solution they were proposing. Then, it was Jordan's turn.

Hannah, who had been standing by, moved to his side, holding up an mPad so he could read his notes without having to twist or strain his neck to see the main screen. This left Jordan's hands free to clutch his heart pillow, bracing his sternum as he faced his classmates.

He spoke with a quiet, steady conviction. This wasn't just an assignment; it was his life. "The current map isn't just inaccurate," he said, his voice finding its strength. "It's a barrier. When I arrived here, I spent my first weeks lost because the resources I needed weren't on any map". He spoke of his personal experiences trying to find elevators, push button doors, and accessible routes—like the one in Bennett Hall—that were completely undocumented. "Our proposal isn't about spending millions on new construction. It's about providing accurate information. It's about telling students where the tools to succeed *already* are."

When he finished, a respectful, impressed applause filled the room. The entire Group of 8, standing with him, was beaming with pride.

They took their seats as a group and stayed for the rest of the 50-minute class, listening to the other presentations. When the professor dismissed them, Dr. Evans came over to Jordan, his expression full of warmth.

"Mr. Fuller, that was exceptional," he said. "I am so proud of how far you've come. Just to confirm, your accommodation paperwork is all set. You're clear to complete the rest of the semester remotely".

"Thank you, Dr. Evans," Jordan said, feeling a huge weight lift from his shoulders. "For everything."

In the hallway, the Group of 8 huddled for a quick, emotional goodbye. His presentation was over, and they had to run to their next classes. One by one, the pact of five gave him proud, loving kisses, and Mark and Hannah gave him careful, strong hugs.

He was sad to leave. This one hour of normalcy, of being a student with his friends, was the best he'd felt in weeks. He watched them hurry down the hall. He turned his wheelchair, and Megan was there, waiting by the building's entrance, her own face full of pride. It was time to go home and rest.

### Part 5: The System Crash

Megan wheeled Jordan back through the bustling campus to her car, which was still in the perfect handicap spot. The walk was quiet; Jordan was lost in his own thoughts, the adrenaline of the presentation fading. She helped him with the careful, practiced transfer into the front passenger seat, settled his heart pillow against his chest, and buckled him in.

She walked around to the driver's side and slid into her seat. She put the key in the ignition but paused for a moment, letting out a satisfied sigh. "You did so good, Jordan. I was so proud of you."

She turned to look at him, but he wasn't looking at her. He was staring through the windshield at Walton Hall, at the students milling about, backpacks on, heading to their next class.

He had just tasted it. For fifty minutes, he had been a normal student again. He had been with his friends, participating, *winning*. And now, he had to leave. He had to go back to the basement, back to being a patient.

His whole world collapsed.

"I want to go back," he whispered, his voice trembling. "I want to go to my next class".

"Jordan, we can't," Megan said gently. "The plan was just for this one..."

"NO!" he suddenly roared, the sound shocking in the small car. "I want to go back!"

He began to thrash in the seat, his body tensing. A low, guttural sound, the one Daniel had warned them about, ripped from his chest as his autistic meltdown took over.

Megan’s blood ran cold. He was going to pop his stitches. He was going to break the wires. This wasn't a meltdown they could ride out; this was a medical emergency, and she was "alone".

"Jordan, no! Stop!" she commanded, her voice high with panic. "Your chest! You have to stop tensing!"

But he was gone, lost in the storm, his body arching against the seatbelt.

She had seconds. She couldn't grab him; she'd pull on his chest. She couldn't just yell; he couldn't hear her. She had to *ground* him.

In a desperate, instinctive move, Megan unbuckled her own seatbelt, threw herself across the console, and straddled his lap, pinning his lower body against the seat with her own weight. It was a shocking, intimate act, but it left his chest completely free.

"Jordan! Listen to my voice!" she screamed, her face inches from his. She grabbed his shoulders, her fingers digging in, applying firm, steady pressure *away* from his sternum. "You are safe! But you are going to hurt yourself! You MUST stop tensing! Squeeze my hands! Squeeze them, NOW!"

She peeled his hands off his pillow and forced them to grip hers, pushing all her strength into his. "Focus on my hands, Jordan! Not your chest! My hands! You are safe! I've got you!"

He thrashed, the guttural sound still vibrating, but she held on, her entire body a grounding, desperate shield. She was crying, terrified, but she didn't let go.

"I've got you," she said again, her voice breaking. "I'm right here. You are not alone. I've got you."

Slowly, agonizingly, the pressure began to recede. The thrashing lessened. The horrible, low-frequency sound in his chest subsided, replaced by a deep, shuddering, painful sob.

He was back. He was crying, his body trembling with the aftershocks, but he was no longer rigid.

Megan, shaking so hard she could barely breathe, didn't move. She just collapsed against him, her head on his shoulder, her arms still wrapped around him, her legs still pinning him safely. She held him, her own tears of terror and relief soaking his shirt, as he cried into her hair.

"It's okay," she sobbed, her voice muffled. "You're okay. I've got you. I'm not letting go."

She had done it. She had calmed the storm, all by herself. And in the process, in that terrifying, desperate moment, she had become his safe person.

### Part 6: The New Safe Person

The ride from CPI back to Christiansburg was heavy with the aftershock of the meltdown. Megan, having calmed Jordan down to a state of exhausted, tearful quiet, drove with both hands gripping the wheel, her own adrenaline slowly ebbing, leaving her shaking. Jordan just stared out the passenger window, his heart pillow clutched to his chest, his mind a total blank. He was mortified, but also, for the first time in his life, he felt a new kind of safety. She hadn't run. She hadn't yelled *at* him. She had dived into the storm with him and pulled him out.

When they got to the Brooks' house, Megan helped him transfer from the passenger seat to his wheelchair. She didn't say a word, just wheeled him around the side of the house, down the grassy hill to the walk-out basement's sliding glass door.

Once they were inside, the silence of the empty basement felt charged. Jordan stopped his chair, his hands trembling. He looked at Megan, his eyes shining with unshed tears. He needed to be grounded again, but this time, it was different. He didn't just need a caregiver; he wanted *her*.

"Megan," he whispered, his voice hoarse. "Can we... can we cuddle? Please?"

He wanted to hold her, to show her, without words, that she was one of them now.

Megan's expression softened instantly, her own fear melting away in the face of his need. "Of course, Jordan."

She helped him transfer from his wheelchair to the sectional sofa, his body moving with a careful, pained stiffness. He lay down, and she sat at the end, letting him rest his head in her lap, just as she had done that first morning. He immediately turned, wrapping an arm around her waist, holding her lovingly, his face pressed into her side. She rested her hand in his hair, the two of them cuddling safely, his chest protected.

They sat in silence for a long time. He finally broke it, his voice muffled.

"You... you're like them," he stammered, trying to find the words. "Like Aubrie, and Madi, and Zoe".

Megan's hand stilled in his hair. Her heart gave a painful, hopeful lurch. *Will she / won't she...*

"You're... you're one of my safe people now," he continued, struggling. "I... I just mean... the pact... you fit. You could... if you wanted...".

He was trying to offer her a spot, to tell her she was welcome.

But Megan didn't pick up on it. Or, rather, she *chose* not to. Her internal barrier, the one she had been building for weeks, slammed into place. *He's 19. He's just had a meltdown. He's grateful. He's not... he can't be... asking you to be his girlfriend. You're 27. You're his sister. Don't make this weird*.

She used his fumbled words as a cover, an off-ramp for her own confusing feelings. She gently stroked his hair, her voice calm and sisterly, though her heart was hammering.

"Shh, it's okay, Jordan," she said softly, intentionally misinterpreting him. "I know. I'm part of the family. I'm so happy to be here for you. What you have with the pact is so special, and I'm just... I'm honored to be here to help".

She had defaulted to the older sister role. It was the only one that felt safe. Jordan, hearing her words, felt a small ping of rejection, but he was too exhausted to push. He just nodded, closing his eyes, and held her a little tighter. He was safe, and for now, that was enough.

### Part 7: The Holiday Mixer

The energy in the basement that evening was triumphant. The Group of 8, having returned from their last class, swarmed Jordan on the sofa, all of them talking at once about the presentation.

"You killed it, J!" Mark said, giving him a careful, one-armed brotherly hug. "Dr. Evans looked genuinely impressed."

"He was," Zoe confirmed, her face showing a rare, proud smile. "Your personal testimony provided the emotional framework that the logical data needed. It was an optimal presentation."

Jordan felt a deep, satisfying warmth. He was so happy to be back, so glad he had been able to do it.

As the group's chaotic energy settled, Megan, who had been quietly preparing dinner for everyone in the kitchenette, spoke up.

"So," she said, her voice a little hesitant. "My work sent out the official invite for the big holiday mixer. It's next Friday."

"Are you going?" Hannah asked from the dining table.

"I kind of have to," Megan said. "It's the big in-person event in Roanoke. They're allowing us to bring a guest".

Her mind flashed, unbidden, to Jordan. He was the person she had spent the most time with for weeks, her work-buddy, her new confidant. A tiny, ridiculous part of her wished she could ask *him*. She immediately crushed the thought. It was absurd. He was 19, he was her sister's... *everything*... and more importantly, he was still on strict sternal precautions. He couldn't possibly go to a crowded, standing-room-only corporate party.

On top of all that, she had seen his meltdown in the car today. She knew he needed a lot of grounding to attend crowded events, and a loud, professional mixer with hundreds of strangers was the worst possible environment. She wouldn't be able to provide the kind of total focus he'd need there, not while trying to network with her coworkers.

"So," she finished, her voice a little flat, "I guess I'll just be going by myself".

"You absolutely *should* go," Laura said firmly, having come down the stairs with Daniel.

Aubrie, who was nestled on the sofa next to Jordan, nodded in vigorous agreement. "Megan, you have to go. You've been playing nurse to Jordan for weeks now, cooped up in this basement every single day".

"She's right," Jordan added, looking over at her with a grateful smile. "You deserve a night off. Go. Have fun. Be with your coworkers. I'll be fine, I've got this whole crew to keep me company".

Megan looked at all their enthusiastic, supportive faces. She felt a small pang of guilt for even *wanting* to leave, but she knew they were right. "Okay," she said, a real smile forming. "Okay. I'll go."

### Part 8: The New Variable

Later that Friday night, the basement was full of the quiet energy of the Group of 8 settling in for the weekend. Jordan was on the sofa, his head in Aubrie's lap, watching a movie with the group when the internal stairs door opened.

Megan came down, her nice dress and heels looking out of place in their cozy, domestic space.

"Hey!" Hannah called from the floor, where she was leaning against Mark's legs. "How was it? Did you have fun?"

Megan blushed, a small, genuine smile on her face. "It was... it was actually really nice. I met someone".

The movie was immediately forgotten. "Ooh, details!" Madison said, sitting up.

"His name is Alex," Megan said, her voice a little shy. "He's in the logistics department. He just... he seemed like a perfect gentleman. He was really easy to talk to".

"And?" Lauren prompted, grinning.

"And... he asked me on a proper date for this weekend. And I said yes".

The group, led by Aubrie, let out a small, happy cheer. "Megan, that's great!" Aubrie said, beaming. "You deserve to have a nice date."

Jordan, looking up from Aubrie's lap, smiled. "Yeah, that's awesome, Megan. I'm happy for you."

He meant it, but he also felt a small, strange, and unfamiliar pang in his chest. He quickly identified it and pushed it down.

Megan looked at all their faces—Jordan's, Zoe's, Aubrie's. There was not a trace of jealousy or anger. They were all just genuinely, completely happy for her. It was the most supportive, loving reaction she could have imagined.

Which, for some reason, only made her feel more confused than ever.

## Chapter 15: The Christmas Protocol

### Part 1: The Fortress Gains a Member

Christmas Day was loud, warm, and full of the chaotic, happy energy of the entire Brooks clan. Alex, Megan's new boyfriend, had been polite and charming all through dinner, though he seemed a little stiff, like an outsider observing a strange, foreign culture.

After dinner, as the family was settling in the main living room, Alex and Megan moved to the front entryway for their goodbyes.

Down in the basement, Jordan was resting on the sectional sofa, surrounded by the Group of 8. They were laughing at a movie they had put on, a comfortable, sleepy pile. The peaceful quiet was broken by the sound of muffled, raised voices from the floor above, leaking down the internal staircase.

Jordan tensed, his good mood vanishing. He looked at Zoe, his eyes wide.

"It's just Megan and Alex," Zoe said, her voice calm, though her eyes were narrowed, analyzing the new, disruptive data.

The muffled voices escalated. They couldn't make out the words, just the sharp, begging tone of Alex, and Megan's firm, clear "No."

Then, they all heard it. The unmistakable, sharp *slam* of the front door, vibrating through the house.

A moment later, Megan came down the basement stairs. Her face was pale, and she was visibly shaking, her eyes bright with angry tears.

The movie was immediately forgotten.

"Megan? What happened?" Aubrie asked, jumping up from the sofa.

Megan stood in the middle of the room, her hands clenched. "He... he knew my lease was expiring at the end of January," she said, her voice trembling. "He... he had a key made to his house. He called it my 'real' Christmas present. He said I should just... move in. Tonight."

"What?" Madison said, her voice full of disgust.

"He said *that* was my present, and he... he clearly implied it came with... *other* expectations. Tonight." Megan shook her head, her voice breaking. "I knew I wasn't ready for that. I told him no. I told him I would rather stay here with my family". "And he just... he wouldn't get the hint. So I ended it. I just... I closed the door in his face".

Zoe and Aubrie, seeing their sister was upset, immediately moved in. "Hey," Aubrie said softly, "come here." They gently guided Megan to the sofa, where Jordan was already sitting up, his own face a mask of concern.

"He's a jerk," Jordan said, his voice firm.

"He's an idiot," Aubrie agreed. "Come on, sit."

They had Megan sit on the sofa, and then, in a single, fluid motion, they had her cuddle up with Jordan. He immediately wrapped his arms around her, pulling her into a tight, grounding hug. She buried her face in his shoulder, her body still shaking, and just let herself be held by him.

### Part 2: The Invitation

As the evening wound down, the energy in the basement shifted from crisis to a deep, protective comfort. It was time for bed. The group went through their usual rituals, changing into pajamas and getting ready to sleep.

Aubrie, who usually claimed the single spot next to Jordan in the king bed, finished brushing her teeth. She came out of the bathroom, looked at Megan—who was sitting on the sofa, still looking shaken and lost—and then looked at the rest of the pact. A silent, unanimous decision was made.

"Okay," Aubrie said, her voice soft but firm. "Bedtime."

She walked over to Megan. "And tonight, you're sleeping in the king bed. With Jordan."

Megan's head snapped up, her face a mask of panic. "Oh, no, I... I can't. Aubrie, that's your spot. I'm fine on the sofa. Really. I don't want to intrude".

"It's not about the sofa," Madison said gently, coming over to sit on the coffee table in front of her. "It's about *us*. We want you with him. We want you to be safe. We want you to be comforted".

"But I..." Megan stammered, looking at Jordan, who was watching her with a hopeful, gentle expression. "It's not... I'm 27. He's 19. It's not appropriate. I'm Zoe's sister".

Zoe, who had been listening to her sister's internal barrier, stepped forward. "Megan, your 'age barrier' logic is flawed. Let's analyze the data".

She held up her fingers, ticking off the points.

"One: Jordan is nineteen. He is a legal, consenting adult, a fact that has been established in a court of law". "Two: You are twenty-seven. You are also a legal, consenting adult". "Three: You are upset and in need of comfort after a traumatic event". "Four: Jordan, a safe person, is offering that comfort". "Five: The entire pact, his primary partners, are *insisting* you take that comfort".

Zoe looked her older sister in the eye. "Therefore, the only variable preventing this optimal, supportive outcome is your own, irrelevant social anxiety. You should sleep in the bed".

"She's right," Lauren said, joining the group. "That guy Alex was a jerk because he wouldn't listen to you. We're not him. We're *listening* to what you need, even if you're not saying it."

"We want you here, Megan," Sarah added, her voice soft. "You're family."

Megan looked at Aubrie, her eyes desperate for an out. "But Aubrie... I can't take your place."

Aubrie just smiled, her heart full of bliss. "You're not taking my place, Megan. You're *joining* it. We're welcoming you. This is what we do. We share. This is the pact. Now, are you really going to make Jordan sleep alone after that jerk upset you?"

Megan looked at the five women surrounding her, their faces open, loving, and completely devoid of jealousy. It was an overwhelming, powerful force. She looked over at Jordan, who was holding the blankets back on the empty side of the bed, his expression one of quiet, hopeful invitation. Her internal barrier, the one she had held onto for weeks, finally crumbled under the weight of their acceptance.

"Okay," she whispered, her voice thick with tears. "Okay."

The rest of the pact, their mission accomplished, smiled and headed for their own queen beds on the other side of the room. Megan, still shaking slightly, slipped into the king-sized bed.

Jordan immediately shifted closer, his body warm, and wrapped an arm around her, pulling her close in a non-strenuous, profoundly comforting cuddle.

"It's okay," he whispered. "You're safe here."

She cried into his shoulder, not from sadness, but from overwhelming relief. She was finally, truly, home.

### Part 3: The Pact of Six

It was late, long after midnight. The basement was dark, filled with the soft, steady breathing of the sleeping pact. But in the king-sized bed, Megan was wide awake.

She was lying on her side, and Jordan was cuddled up against her back, his arm draped over her waist, his breathing deep and even. He had been asleep for hours. She, however, couldn't sleep.

Her mind was replaying the entire, bizarre day. The confrontation with Alex, the slammed door, the subsequent, gentle "intervention" by the pact. She thought about the "real Christmas present" Alex had demanded—that cold, arrogant, transactional key. The thing *he* wanted, which he'd tried to force on her.

And now, she was getting what she *actually* wanted.

She was simply sleeping in a bed with a trusted person of the opposite gender. A person who wasn't demanding anything, who wasn't pushing, who just *wanted* her to be there for comfort. The pact, and Jordan, had offered her the one thing Alex couldn't: a safe harbor.

In that dark, quiet moment, Megan suddenly realized she no longer cared about the age difference. She didn't care that he was nineteen. She didn't care that he was post-op and still healing from a massive surgery. She just cared that she was getting warm, safe hugs from a trusted guy who was lying in bed with her.

She sighed, a long, quiet breath of contentment, and shifted slightly.

"You 'wake?" a sleepy voice mumbled from the pillow next to her. Jordan's.

"I can't sleep," Megan whispered, feeling bad for waking him.

"Me neither," a different voice whispered from one of the queen beds. Madison.

"You okay, Meg?" Aubrie's voice, thick with sleep, came from the other side of the king bed, where she had been sleeping before Megan's arrival.

Megan felt a blush creep up her neck in the dark. "Yeah. I'm... I'm really good. This is just... a lot."

"It's a good lot, though," Jordan mumbled, his arm tightening around her waist in a sleepy, reassuring hug.

"Yeah," Megan whispered, her voice thick with emotion. "It really is."

"Good," Aubrie said, her voice a warm, happy rumble. "Now go to sleep, you two."

Megan closed her eyes, a real, genuine smile on her face. She was home. She let the steady rhythm of Jordan's breathing finally pull her under.

### Part 4: The Longest Night

Sleep wouldn't come. Megan lay still, her heart hammering, her stomach full of butterflies. She was acutely aware of Jordan's solid, warm presence cuddled against her back. She had been given *permission* to be here, in this bed, with him. She was terrified of moving, of doing something wrong, of losing this new, incredible level of trust.

Jordan was wide awake, too, though he was pretending to be asleep, listening to her breathing. He couldn't sleep. This felt new, this felt *exciting*. His mind was already racing ahead. He was ready to resume the puppy pile, the full, comforting weight of his entire family, and he was ready to officially welcome Megan into it. But he knew he couldn't. Daniel's "one person" rule was still in effect, and his sternum was still a fragile, healing thing.

He was ready for *everything* again, including the full, strenuous physical intimacy he shared with the pact, but he knew with a deep, frustrating certainty that his doctors would say no.

He felt Megan shift, a tiny, restless movement. He couldn't stand the silence.

"You really can't sleep, can you?" he whispered into the dark.

Megan let out a small, shaky laugh. "No. My brain won't shut up."

"Mine either," he admitted.

From one of the queen beds, a phone screen lit up, illuminating Zoe's face. "The auditory sensors in this room are picking up non-sleep-pattern conversation," she whispered, her voice dry. "Is the new variable causing a system instability?"

"No," Jordan and Megan whispered in unison.

"Good," Zoe's voice came back, and the screen went dark.

A moment of silence, and then Megan and Jordan both started to giggle quietly, trying to stifle the sound in their pillows.

"At least it's Saturday," Jordan whispered, his body finally starting to relax. "No one has to get up early".

"That's good," Megan whispered back, her own tension easing. "Because I have a feeling this is going to be a long night."

They both tried to go back to sleep, but they couldn't. They just lay there, a few inches apart, wide awake and buzzing with a new, shared, and very exciting reality.

### Part 5: The New Protocol

Saturday morning, December 26th, was bright and calm. No one had to get up early for class or work. The group slowly assembled in the basement living room. Jordan was already on the sectional sofa, a comfortable blanket over his legs.

Megan was the last to emerge, feeling shy and uncertain after the events of the previous night. She had slept in the king bed, cuddled against Jordan, and it had felt more right than anything in her life. But now, in the light of day, her anxieties came flooding back. *Was it a one-time thing? Was she just the pity case?*

She went to the kitchenette to start making coffee, keeping her back to the room.

"Megan? Can you come sit with us?"

It was Aubrie's voice. Megan turned. The other five women of the pact were all gathered, sitting on the sectional and the armchairs around Jordan. It felt like an intervention.

"Am I... in trouble?" Megan asked, her voice small.

"In trouble?" Aubrie laughed, a warm, gentle sound. "Megan, no, you’re not in trouble. We just... we need to talk. Formally."

Megan nervously took a seat in the armchair opposite Jordan.

"First of all," Aubrie said, her gaze soft and steady, "how are you feeling? After that... *jerk* Alex last night."

"I'm... okay," Megan said. "I'm just glad he's gone. And I'm so sorry if I brought all that drama here."

"You didn't," Madison said firmly from the other side of the sofa. "He did. And you're one of us. You're family. You bring *nothing* here but you."

Megan looked down, her heart hammering. "I... I still feel weird about last night. About the bed. I know I'm just Zoe's sister, and I'm so much older than all of you, and I don't want to make things... weird".

Zoe, who had been listening intently, finally spoke. "Megan, your 'age barrier' logic is flawed. Let's analyze the data".

She leaned forward, her expression serious. "One: Jordan is nineteen. He is a legal, consenting adult, a fact that has been established in a court of law. Two: You are twenty-seven. You are also a legal, consenting adult. Three: The existing pact of five, which holds 100% of the social and romantic equity in this relationship, is giving its full, unanimous blessing. Four: Jordan is clearly reciprocating the emotional bond. Therefore, the eight-year age difference is an irrelevant variable".

"What Zoe is trying to say," Lauren chimed in, smiling, "is that we see the way you look at him. And we see the way he looks at you."

"We've been waiting for you to catch up," Sarah added softly. "You just... you fit, Megan."

Megan looked at Aubrie, her eyes wide with disbelief. "You mean... you all... you *want* me to... to join the pact?"

"We want you to be part of this family, in whatever way makes you happy," Aubrie said. "And that means we need to teach you the rules. Because you're not an outsider. You're one of us now. Which means, first of all..."

Aubrie stood up, walked over to Megan, and gently pulled her from the armchair. She sat her on the sofa, right next to Jordan.

"It means," Aubrie continued, "that you are allowed to be romantic with him. 100%. We *want* you to. And I'm not talking about a sisterly kiss on the cheek. I mean *kiss* him".

Megan stared at her, her entire body frozen in a state of hopeful shock.

"He's right here," Aubrie said, her face radiating pure bliss. She looked at Jordan. "Do you want to kiss Megan?"

Jordan, who had been watching this all unfold with a look of pure adoration, just nodded, his eyes locked on Megan. "More than anything," he whispered.

"Go on," Madison encouraged from his other side. "It's okay. We're all right here. There is no jealousy in this room".

Megan's hands were shaking. She looked at Jordan, at his soft, waiting expression. Slowly, she leaned in. He met her halfway. Their first, real, romantic kiss was gentle, hesitant, and full of all the unsaid things from the past few weeks. Then, as she felt him relax, it deepened. It was a long, slow, loving kiss, and when they finally pulled apart, Megan was breathless. She looked around. The other four women were just smiling.

"See?" Lauren said. "No lightning bolts. Just us."

"Now," Aubrie said, sitting back down, "for the second rule. The one with the medical constraint."

"What Zoe means," Madison picked up, her voice practical, "is that this pact also includes sex. Once Jordan is recovered. He's already had sex with all five of us. We all know about it. It's part of the agreement".

"And just so you know, as a practical matter," Zoe added, her voice clinical and non-judgmental, "all five of us are on birth control. It's how we can have a sexual relationship with Jordan without worrying about pregnancy right now, before we're ready".

"We'd suggest you get on it, too," Sarah added softly. "Just so you're ready, for when *he's* ready".

"But that's the key," Aubrie stressed, her voice firm, "he's not ready *right now*. He is on strict sternal precautions. He cannot do anything strenuous. It's not safe. So that is 100% off the table, for *all* of us, until his doctor gives him the all-clear in a few weeks".

"We just need you to know," Lauren said, "that when that day comes, the invitation extends to you, too. Fully. With our complete blessing. No jealousy. Ever".

Megan just stared at the five of them, and at Jordan, tears streaming down her face.

"I... I don't know what to say," she whispered.

Jordan took her hand, his thumb stroking her knuckles. "Just say yes," he said, his voice thick with emotion.

Megan looked at him, then at her sister Zoe, at Aubrie, at Madison, at Lauren, at Sarah. Her new family. "Yes," she cried, and this time, when she kissed him, it wasn't hesitant at all.

### Part 6: The Final Permission

Megan's heart was hammering. Jordan was still holding her hand, his eyes shining with a love that was no longer hesitant. She looked at the five other women, expecting... she didn't know what. A flicker of jealousy? A hint of buyer's remorse?

She saw nothing but joy.

"Well," Madison said, breaking the silence, her voice full of a playful grin. "That was a good start. A little... polite, but good."

Megan blushed, confused. "What... what do you mean?"

"She means," Aubrie said, her smile so warm it melted the last of Megan's anxiety, "that you're still acting like you're in trouble. You're not. You're one of us now. You're allowed to *really* kiss him."

"We're not just 'okay' with it, Megan," Lauren added gently. "We're *happy* about it. We've been watching you two dance around this for weeks. It was getting painful."

Megan looked at Jordan, who was watching her with an expression of pure adoration. He was her safe person. He was the one who had made her feel wanted again. And this entire family was giving her their blessing.

"Go on," Madison encouraged, her voice soft. "Kiss him like you mean it."

Jordan, his confidence bolstered by the full support of his pact, didn't wait. He leaned in again, and this time, Megan met him with a new certainty. This kiss wasn't hesitant. It was a deep, passionate, and explicitly romantic kiss, a full and loving exploration.

When they finally broke for air, Megan was breathless. She looked up at the pact of five, her mind braced for the inevitable sting of jealousy that all her life experience told her *must* be there.

But there was none. Aubrie was beaming. Zoe was giving her a small, satisfied nod. Madison, Lauren, and Sarah were all smiling, their faces full of nothing but pure, uncomplicated happiness for their two friends.

Megan couldn't believe it. She had just tongue-kissed Jordan, passionately, right in front of his five other girlfriends, and they were *happy* about it.

That was the final piece. The last of her social conditioning, her fear of the age gap, her anxiety about "stealing" him, all of it evaporated. This was real. This was the pact. And she was, finally, a part of it.

Her mind immediately went to the rule Zoe and Sarah had mentioned. The practical part. The responsible part. She, like them, was now in a sexual relationship with Jordan, even if it was currently on a medical hold.

Okay, she thought, her mind clear for the first time in weeks. Okay. I'll call my OB/GYN on Monday. I need to make an appointment to get on birth control. I'm part of this now, and I'm going to be responsible about it.

### Part 7: The Lesson

Megan was still reeling, her mind trying to process the fact that she had just passionately tongue-kissed Jordan in front of his five other girlfriends, and they had applauded.

"See?" Aubrie said, her voice soft. She was sitting on the other side of Jordan, and she took his hand. "This is the pact. This is how it works. No jealousy. Just... more family. More love."

To prove the point, Aubrie leaned in. Jordan, without hesitation, turned his head and gave her a deep, loving kiss, just as passionate as the one he had given Megan. Megan watched, her mind braced for... something. A flicker of triumph from Aubrie? A look of possession?

There was nothing. Just love.

When they parted, Madison, who was perched on the armchair, grinned. "Okay, my turn before he gets tired."

She leaned over, and Jordan met her halfway. They shared a long, familiar, romantic kiss. Again, Megan watched. No jealousy.

Lauren and Sarah, who were sitting together on the floor, were next. "Us, too," Lauren said, and they both moved in. Jordan gave each of them a loving, intimate kiss in turn, his gaze warm and affectionate for both of them.

Megan was stunned. Her entire concept of relationships was being rewritten in real-time.

Finally, there was only Zoe.

Jordan turned to her. Megan’s stomach did a backflip. *Okay, this is the real test,* she thought, her old anxieties flaring. *That's her sister. He just kissed me, he just kissed them, and now...* She was expecting Zoe, her logical, analytical sister, to be disgusted, or at least awkward.

Zoe simply leaned forward from her spot at the coffee table. "My data indicates it's my turn," she said, a small, rare, teasing smile on her lips.

Jordan smiled and met her kiss. It was just as romantic, just as deep, and just as full of love as the others.

When they pulled back, Jordan looked flushed and happy. Zoe, however, looked completely unfazed. She just looked at Jordan, then turned her analytical gaze to her sister. She wasn't angry. She wasn't disgusted. She just looked... proud. She gave Megan a small, validating nod.

Megan's world tilted on its axis. The last, final wall of her old social conditioning crumbled. It was real. No jealousy. No competition. Just... love.

### Part 8: The No Privacy Protocol

The room was full of a warm, loving energy. Megan was still sitting next to Jordan on the sofa, her hand in his, her mind reeling from the passionate, jealous-free kisses they had all just shared.

The moment was finally broken by Madison, who clapped her hands together. "Okay!" she said cheerfully. "As much fun as this is, I'm starving for a *real* breakfast, and we're all still in our pajamas. Time to get dressed for the day".

Before Megan could even process what that meant, the other four women of the original pact—Aubrie, Zoe, Lauren, and Sarah—simply stood up and began to change. Right there, in the middle of the living room. They slipped out of their sleep shorts and t-shirts, completely naked for a moment as they chatted about what to wear, then casually pulled on fresh underwear, bras, jeans, and sweaters from their dressers.

Megan just stared, her face flooding with a hot blush. She knew about the "no privacy" rule, but seeing it in action was another thing entirely. No one was hiding. No one was turning their back. It was the most natural, normal thing in the world to them.

"Jordan, you need help?" Aubrie asked, pulling a comb through her hair.

"I can get my shirt," Jordan said. He was still on the sofa. He carefully, wincing at his sternum, pulled his pajama shirt over his head. "But I'll need help with my pants".

He managed to get his legs into his underwear and jeans, but as always, he couldn't get them up past his hips from a seated position. "Okay... I'm stuck," he said, looking up.

Aubrie, who was about to help, paused. She looked at Megan, who was still sitting on the sofa, the only other person still in pajamas. Aubrie smiled, a warm, knowing, and inviting smile.

"Megan? Do you mind?" she asked, her voice gentle. "You're right there."

This was it. This was the next test. This wasn't a clinical shower. This was... *partner* care. Megan's heart hammered, but she looked at Aubrie's trusting face, and at Jordan, who was looking at her with that same, simple, uncomplicated trust.

"Yeah, of course," she whispered.

She knelt on the floor in front of him. "Okay," she said, her voice a little shaky. "What do you need?"

"Just... pull 'em up?" he said. "I can't stand and pull at the same time, and I can't twist."

She took the waistband of his underwear and his jeans. Her hands brushed his bare skin as she gently, firmly, eased the fabric up over his hips. He held onto her shoulders to balance. It was an act of pure, domestic intimacy. She fastened his button, her fingers brushing his stomach.

"Got it," she said, her voice breathless.

"Thanks, Megan," he said, his smile so full of love it made her butterflies take flight all over again.

She stood up. And now, she was the only one in the room still in pajamas. The other five women were all dressed, watching her with kind, expectant smiles.

Okay, she thought. This is my family now.

She took a deep, shaky breath. She pulled her own sleep shirt over her head. No one leered. No one made it weird. Aubrie just handed her the clean t-shirt she'd left on the dresser.

"Welcome to the pact, Megan," Aubrie said, her voice full of bliss.

With Daniel and Laura already out for the day, having left a note that they were heading over to the construction site to check on the progress of the new compound, this left the Group of 8 to themselves.

"Okay," Megan announced, swinging her legs off the sofa, a new, confident energy in her voice. "I'm starving. And since I'm the new roommate, I'm cooking breakfast for everyone."

"You don't have to do that, Meg," Hannah said, stifling a yawn from the armchair.

"I want to," Megan insisted. She looked at Jordan, who was sitting on the edge of the king bed, a soft smile on his face. "And it's going to be heart-healthy, so we're all on the same page."

Zoe, seeing her sister take charge, immediately moved to the kitchenette to assist. "A sound logistical plan," she said, pulling a large mixing bowl from the cabinet. "What's the protocol?"

"Oatmeal pancakes," Megan declared, pulling a recipe up on her mPhone. "Made with unsweetened applesauce instead of oil. And I'll make a huge batch of scrambled egg whites with spinach".

The two sisters began to cook, their movements efficient and practiced in the small space. The rest of the group relaxed in the living room, the comforting sounds of cooking and the smell of breakfast filling the basement. Jordan, now settled in his wheelchair, watched Megan, his heart full. This was his new family, his new pact of six, and his new sister, all in one.

### Part 9: A Health Firewall for Jordan

The conversation happened quietly one evening in the Brooks' basement during the Winter Break of 2015. Jordan was still in the early, painful stages of his recovery from open-heart surgery, and his world was the sectional sofa. He was still on strict sternal precautions, a constant, aching reminder of his own fragility.

The seven of them—Jordan, Aubrie, Madison, Zoe, Lauren, Sarah, and Megan—were gathered in the living area. The rest of the group was watching a movie, but Jordan was quiet, his mind clearly somewhere else. He had been thinking all day about the CVICU, about the ventilator.

"Hey," he said, his voice quiet, cutting through the movie's dialogue. The group immediately muted the TV.

"I was just thinking," Jordan said, his voice raspy. "When I was in the hospital... when I was on the ventilator... if something had gone wrong, who would the doctors have listened to? Who is my legal next-of-kin?"

A cold, heavy silence fell over the room. They all knew the answer. It was *her*.

"He's right," Zoe said, her voice sharp and analytical. "We need a legal firewall. His mother has proven she is a persistent threat. Jordan needs a lawfully married spouse. For power of attorney. For medical decisions. To legally and permanently revoke Aubrie Sinclair's access to him."

"But that's the part that's so unfair," Jordan said, his autistic frustration surfacing. The logic was infuriating. "The law is illogical. It doesn't account for a family like ours. Polygamy is illegal. I can't marry all of you. But I *want* to. You are all my coequals."

"It *is* unfair," Aubrie agreed, her own autistic mind hating the inefficient, arbitrary rule.

"It may be unfair, but it's the law," Zoe countered. "We have to choose one person for the paperwork."

A new quiet fell over the group as they processed the weight of this. Jordan looked at the faces of the six women he loved. How could he choose?

It was Madison who broke the silence. She shifted from her spot on the floor, propping herself up on an elbow to look directly at Aubrie.

"It has to be you, Aubrie," she said, her voice soft but certain.

Aubrie looked surprised, her brow furrowed. "Mads, why? We're all..." She trailed off, but her thought was clear in the eyes of everyone present: *We're all in love with him as coequals. The pact is six, not one.*

"Because you were first," Madison said, her voice full of a fierce, protective love. "That very first night. When he was so broken and scared he couldn't even speak."

Megan, who was cuddled on Jordan's other side on the sofa, nodded, her voice thick with emotion. "She's right, Aubrie. The rest of us... we're the house. But you're the foundation. It's the only thing that's logical."

*Broken?* The word echoed in Jordan's mind, a strange and distant descriptor. He didn't feel broken. He felt whole, strong, surrounded by a love so complete it had rebuilt him from the ground up. He looked down at his own hands, steady and sure, and realized with a jolt that he hadn't seen that shy, terrified boy in the mirror for a very long time.

Madison continued, her voice unwavering. "You were the one who crawled into that bed and just held him. You didn't ask questions, you didn't try to fix him. You were just... there. You were the first person to show him an ounce of kindness in his entire life. That's a place none of the rest of us can ever claim. It's only right that it's you."

Tears welled in Aubrie's eyes as she looked at Madison, a wave of overwhelming gratitude washing over her.

Jordan reached out, his hand covering both of theirs. He looked from Madison's clear, steady gaze to Aubrie's tear-streaked face, his heart so full it felt like it might burst.

"I love you both," he whispered. He then looked around at the other four women, his gaze lingering on each of them. "I love all six of you. So much. And I am so, so grateful that this... us... works. That there's no jealousy, no heartache, no confusion or competition. Just this."

"We will always be coequals," Zoe said, her voice firm with conviction. "That never changes."

"But Madison's right," Lauren added softly, and Sarah nodded in agreement. "That first night... that's the reason. It has to be."

Jordan took a deep, painful breath, his chest aching. His decision was made, driven by the fresh trauma of his surgery. He looked at Aubrie. "They're right. It has to be you. When I was in that hospital, I was terrified. If I am ever helpless like that again... I need *you* to be the one making my medical decisions. I need you to be the firewall that protects me, and our family, from *her*."

And so, surrounded by the warmth and weight of their collective love, they all agreed. It was their path forward. They would all remain coequals in love, life, and intimacy (once his sternum healed), but when the time came, Aubrie would be the one to legally marry Jordan. The reason was singular and sacred: she was the one who had climbed into bed and comforted a scared, broken boy on his very first night of freedom, an act of kindness that had planted the seed for the extraordinary family that had bloomed around them. It was a foundation that could never be equaled.

### Part 10: The New Identity

After the pact had agreed that Aubrie would be the one to legally marry Jordan, a heavy silence settled over the group. Jordan, still resting on the sofa, looked down at his hands, his anxiety returning.

"I'll marry her," he said, his voice quiet but firm. "But... I won't give her my name."

The group looked confused. "J, what do you mean?" Madison asked gently. "Normally, the bride takes the groom's name".

"I don't care," Jordan said, his voice hardening with an adamancy they hadn't heard before. "I hate that name. 'Aubrey' is *her* name. 'Fuller' is the name of a father I never knew. I am adamant that I want to shed both of them".

This was a new, complex problem. If he married Aubrie, she would become "Aubrie Fuller," legally adopting the very name he was trying to destroy.

Mark, who had been sitting next to Hannah, had been quiet, contemplating his own future with her. He looked at Jordan, his brother, struggling with this identity trap.

"So don't give her your name," Mark said, his voice cutting through the silence.

Everyone turned to him.

"It's 2015, guys," Mark said. "It's just paperwork. What if Aubrie just... doesn't change her name?" He looked at Aubrie. "You just stay 'Aubrie Kelly.'"

Then he turned back to Jordan. "And *you* change yours. You go to court, you file the paperwork, and you legally change your name to whatever you want".

Jordan stared at him. "Change... my name?"

"Yeah, man," Mark said, a warm, brotherly smile spreading across his face. "You want to be 'Jordan Kelly'? Do it. You're an adult. You can."

Jordan processed this. Jordan Kelly. It felt right. But... "My middle name," Jordan whispered. "Jordan is my middle name. I'd... I'd be 'Jordan Kelly.' I wouldn't have a middle name."

Mark's smile widened. He hadn't just been thinking about his future; he'd been thinking about their family. "I've got an extra," he said quietly. "If you want it. It's 'Shawn'".

The room went silent.

"Jordan... Shawn... Kelly," Jordan tested the name, his voice thick with emotion. He was shedding the identity of his abuser (Aubrey) and the name of the father he never knew (Fuller) and adopting the names of his wife (Kelly) and his brother (Shawn).

He looked at Mark, his eyes shining. "Jordan Shawn Kelly," he said, his voice firm. "Yes."

A wave of joyous agreement swept the room. The entire group of eleven—the Group of 8, Megan, and Daniel and Laura, who had been listening from the stairs—all loved the idea. It was perfect.

Hannah, who had been holding Mark's hand, was crying softly, her heart full. She looked at Mark, then at Jordan and Aubrie.

"You know," she said, her voice watery but happy, "we've been talking about this too. Mark and I. Our future."

She looked at Mark, who nodded, giving her the floor.

"We're so in love," she said, her gaze fixed on her boyfriend. "And you two," she looked at Jordan and Aubrie, "are the foundation of this whole family. What if... what if we did it together?"

"What do you mean?" Aubrie asked.

"A double wedding," Hannah beamed. "All of us. The four of us. Mark and I get married in the same ceremony that you and Jordan do". She pictured it. "Two brides and two grooms at the front of the aisle, exchanging vows, and getting legally married at the same time".

The idea was brilliant. It wasn't just Jordan's legal protection; it was a celebration of the two core, stable relationships that anchored their entire world.

The entire group loved the idea. It was the perfect plan.
